      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mauritania" title="Geography of Mauritania">Geography of Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritania_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Mauritania_Topography.png/220px-Mauritania_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Mauritania_Topography.png/330px-Mauritania_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Mauritania_Topography.png/440px-Mauritania_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1843" data-file-height="1876"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritania_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topography of Mauritania
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritania is in the western region of the continent of Africa, and is generally flat, its 1,030,700 square kilometres forming vast, arid plains broken by occasional ridges and clifflike outcroppings.<sup id="cite_ref-SchlÃ¼ter2008_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchlÃ¼ter2008-65">[65]</a></sup> It borders the North <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SchlÃ¼ter2008_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchlÃ¼ter2008-65">[65]</a></sup> It is considered part of both the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a>. A series of scarps face southwest, longitudinally bisecting these plains in the center of the country. The scarps also separate a series of sandstone plateaus, the highest of which is the <a href="/wiki/Adrar_Plateau" title="Adrar Plateau">Adrar Plateau</a>, reaching an elevation of 500 metres.<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes1992_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes1992-66">[66]</a></sup> Spring-fed oases lie at the foot of some of the scarps. Isolated peaks, often rich in minerals, rise above the plateaus; the smaller peaks are called guelbs and the larger ones kedias. The concentric <a href="/wiki/Guelb_er_Richat" class="mw-redirect" title="Guelb er Richat">Guelb er Richat</a> is a prominent feature of the north-central region. <a href="/wiki/Kediet_ej_Jill" title="Kediet ej Jill">Kediet ej Jill</a>, near the city of <a href="/wiki/Zou%C3%AEr%C3%A2t" class="mw-redirect" title="ZouÃ®rÃ¢t">ZouÃ®rÃ¢t</a>, has an elevation of 1,000 metres and is the highest peak. </p>
      <p>Approximately three-quarters of Mauritania is desert or semidesert.<sup id="cite_ref-Wane2009_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wane2009-67">[67]</a></sup> As a result of extended, severe drought, the desert has been expanding since the mid-1960s. The plateaus gradually descend toward the northeast to the barren <a href="/wiki/El_Djouf" title="El Djouf">El Djouf</a>, or "Empty Quarter," a vast region of large sand dunes that merges into the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a>. To the west, between the ocean and the plateaus, are alternating areas of clayey plains (regs) and sand dunes (ergs), some of which shift from place to place, gradually moved by high winds. The dunes generally increase in size and mobility toward the north. </p>
      <p>Belts of natural vegetation, corresponding to the rainfall pattern, extend from east to west and range from traces of tropical forest along the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal_River" class="mw-redirect" title="SÃ©nÃ©gal River">SÃ©nÃ©gal River</a> to brush and savanna in the southeast. Only sandy desert is found in the centre and north of the country. Mauritania is home to seven terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_Acacia_savanna" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahelian Acacia savanna">Sahelian Acacia savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Sudanian_savanna" title="West Sudanian savanna">West Sudanian savanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saharan_halophytics" title="Saharan halophytics">Saharan halophytics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_desert" title="Atlantic coastal desert">Atlantic coastal desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Saharan_steppe_and_woodlands" title="North Saharan steppe and woodlands">North Saharan steppe and woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Saharan_steppe_and_woodlands" title="South Saharan steppe and woodlands">South Saharan steppe and woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Saharan_montane_xeric_woodlands" title="West Saharan montane xeric woodlands">West Saharan montane xeric woodlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Richat_Structure" title="Richat Structure">Richat Structure</a>, dubbed the "Eye of the Sahara", is a formation of rock resembling concentric circles in the <a href="/wiki/Adrar_Plateau" title="Adrar Plateau">Adrar Plateau</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Ouadane" title="Ouadane">Ouadane</a>, westâ€“central <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Mauritania</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Mauritania" title="Wildlife of Mauritania">Wildlife of Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mauritania" title="Economy of Mauritania">Economy of Mauritania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Mauritania" title="Transport in Mauritania">Transport in Mauritania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Mauritania" title="List of power stations in Mauritania">List of power stations in Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritania_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mauritania_treemap.png/220px-Mauritania_treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mauritania_treemap.png/330px-Mauritania_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mauritania_treemap.png/440px-Mauritania_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="868"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritania_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Mauritania's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite being rich in natural resources, Mauritania has a low GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-Dept.2015_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dept.2015-69">[69]</a></sup> A majority of the population still depends on agriculture and livestock for a livelihood, even though most of the nomads and many subsistence farmers were forced into the cities by recurrent droughts in the 1970s and 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Dept.2015_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dept.2015-69">[69]</a></sup> Mauritania has extensive deposits of iron ore, which account for almost 50% of total exports. Gold and copper mining companies are opening mines in the interior. </p>
      <p>The country's first <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Deepwater port">deepwater port</a> opened near <a href="/wiki/Nouakchott" title="Nouakchott">Nouakchott</a> in 1986. In recent years, drought and economic mismanagement have resulted in a buildup of foreign debt. In March 1999, the government signed an agreement with a joint <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>-<a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> mission on a $54&nbsp;million enhanced structural adjustment facility (ESAF). Privatization remains one of the key issues. Mauritania is unlikely to meet ESAF's annual GDP growth objectives of 4â€“5%. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> was discovered in Mauritania in 2001 in the offshore <a href="/wiki/Chinguetti_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinguetti field">Chinguetti field</a>. Although potentially significant for the Mauritanian economy, its overall influence is difficult to predict. Mauritania has been described as a "desperately poor desert nation, which straddles the Arab and African worlds and is Africa's newest, if small-scale, oil producer."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> There may be additional oil reserves inland in the <a href="/wiki/Taoudeni_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Taoudeni basin">Taoudeni basin</a>, although the harsh environment will make extraction expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United Arab Emirates government, via its pilot green city <a href="/wiki/Masdar" title="Masdar">Masdar</a>, installed new solar plants supply an additional 16.6 megawatts of electricity. The plants will power about 39,000 homes and save 27,850 tonnes of carbon emissions per year.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Mauritania is ranked second in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index), making it potentially one of the main winners in the global transition to renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Mauritania" title="Human rights in Mauritania">Human rights in Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png/200px-Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png/300px-Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png/400px-Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mauritanian blogger and political prisoner <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Cheikh_Ould_Mkhaitir" title="Mohamed Cheikh Ould Mkhaitir">Mohamed Cheikh Ould Mkhaitir</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Abdallahi government was widely perceived as corrupt and restricted access to government information. Sexism, racism, <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, child labour, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Mauritania" title="Human trafficking in Mauritania">human trafficking</a>, and the political marginalization of largely southern-based ethnic groups continued to be problems.<sup id="cite_ref-ussdhr07_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ussdhr07-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Mauritania" title="LGBT rights in Mauritania">Homosexuality</a> is illegal and is a <a href="/wiki/Capital_offense" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital offense">capital offence</a> in Mauritania.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the 2008 coup, the military government of Mauritania faced severe international sanctions and internal unrest. <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> accused it of practicing coordinated torture against criminal and political detainees.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Amnesty has accused the Mauritanian legal system, both before and after the 2008 coup, of functioning with complete disregard for legal procedure, fair trial, or humane imprisonment. The organization has said that the Mauritanian government has practiced institutionalized and continuous use of torture throughout its post-independence history, under all its leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> in 2008 alleged that torture was common in Mauritania, stating that its usage is "deeply anchored in the culture of the security forces", which use it "as a system of investigation and repression". Forms of torture employed include cigarette burns, electric shocks and sexual violence, stated Amnesty International.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> identified torture by Mauritanian law enforcement as one of the "central human rights problems" in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Juan_E._M%C3%A9ndez" title="Juan E. MÃ©ndez">Juan E. MÃ©ndez</a>, an independent expert on human rights from the United Nations, reported in 2016 that legal protections against torture were present but not applied in Mauritania, pointing to an "almost total absence of investigations into allegations of torture".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the US State Department <i>2010 Human Rights Report</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-StateDept-2010_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateDept-2010-85">[85]</a></sup> abuses in Mauritania include: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p>...mistreatment of detainees and prisoners; security force impunity; lengthy pretrial detention; harsh prison conditions; arbitrary arrests; limits on freedom of the press and assembly; corruption; discrimination against women; female genital mutilation (FGM); child marriage; political marginalization of southern-based ethnic groups; racial and ethnic discrimination; slavery and slavery-related practices; and child labor.</p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_slavery">Modern slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Modern slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Mauritania" title="Slavery in Mauritania">Slavery in Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_contemporary_Africa" title="Slavery in contemporary Africa">Slavery</a> persists in Mauritania, despite it being outlawed.<sup id="cite_ref-unspeakable_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unspeakable-86">[86]</a></sup> It is the result of a historical <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a> system, resulting in descent-based slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-unspeakable_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unspeakable-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peyton_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peyton-87">[87]</a></sup> Those enslaved are darker-skinned <a href="/wiki/Haratin" title="Haratin">Haratin</a>, with their owners being lighter-skinned Moors.<sup id="cite_ref-Peyton_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peyton-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1905, the French colonial administration declared an end of slavery in Mauritania, with very little success.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Although nominally abolished in 1981, it was not illegal to own slaves until 2007. </p>
      <p>The US State Department <i>2010 Human Rights Report</i> states, "Government efforts were not sufficient to enforce the antislavery law. No cases have been successfully prosecuted under the antislavery law despite the fact that de facto slavery exists in Mauritania."<sup id="cite_ref-StateDept-2010_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateDept-2010-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, it was estimated that 10% to 20% of the population of Mauritania (between 340,000 and 680,000 people) live in slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, a government minister stated that slavery "no longer exists" in Mauritania.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> However, according to the <a href="/wiki/Walk_Free_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Walk Free Foundation">Walk Free Foundation</a>'s Global Slavery Index, there were an estimated 90,000 enslaved people in Mauritania in 2018 or around 2% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-walkfree_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walkfree-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Obstacles to ending slavery in Mauritania include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The difficulty of enforcing any laws in the country's vast desert<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Poverty that limits opportunities for slaves to support themselves if freed<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Belief that slavery is part of the natural order of this society.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chinguetti-biblio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chinguetti-biblio.jpg/170px-Chinguetti-biblio.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chinguetti-biblio.jpg/255px-Chinguetti-biblio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Chinguetti-biblio.jpg/340px-Chinguetti-biblio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chinguetti-biblio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a> collection in a library in <a href="/wiki/Chinguetti" title="Chinguetti">Chinguetti</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Mauritanian_cuisine" title="Mauritanian cuisine">Mauritanian cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mauritania" title="Music of Mauritania">Music of Mauritania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Mauritania" title="Sport in Mauritania">Sport in Mauritania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Filming for several documentaries and films has taken place in Mauritania, including <i><a href="/wiki/Fort_Saganne" title="Fort Saganne">Fort Saganne</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fifth_Element" title="The Fifth Element">The Fifth Element</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Winged_Migration" title="Winged Migration">Winged Migration</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Timbuktu_(2014_film)" title="Timbuktu (2014 film)">Timbuktu</a></i> (2014). </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/T%27heydinn" title="T'heydinn">T'heydinn</a> is part of <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moorish</a> oral tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The libraries of Chinguetti contain thousands of medieval manuscripts.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

There are probably former relationships â€“ slavery relationships and familial relationships from old days and of the older generations, maybe, or descendants who wish to continue to be in relationships with descendants of their old masters, for familial reasons, or out of affinity, and maybe also for economic interests. But (slavery) is something that is totally finished. All people are free in Mauritania and this phenomenon no longer exists. And I believe that I can tell you that no one profits from this commerce.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=CNN&amp;rft.atitle=Mauritanian+minister+responds+to+accusations+that+slavery+is+rampant&amp;rft.date=2012-03-17&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fthecnnfreedomproject.blogs.cnn.com%2F2012%2F03%2F17%2Fmauritanian-minister-responds-to-accusations-that-slavery-is-rampant%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMauritania" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
